<p><b>Google LLC</b> is an American <a href="/wiki/Multinational_corporation" title="Multinational corporation">multinational</a> <a href="/wiki/Technology_company" title="Technology company">technology company</a> that specializes in <a href="/wiki/Internet" title="Internet">Internet</a>-related services and products, which include <a href="/wiki/Online_advertising" title="Online advertising">online advertising technologies</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Search_engine" title="Search engine">search engine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cloud_computing" title="Cloud computing">cloud computing</a>, software, and hardware. It is considered one of the <a href="/wiki/Big_Tech" title="Big Tech">Big Five</a> technology companies in the U.S. <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a> industry, alongside <a href="/wiki/Amazon_(company)" title="Amazon (company)">Amazon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Facebook,_Inc." title="Facebook, Inc.">Facebook</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[10]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[12]</a></sup>
</p><p>Google was founded in September 1998 by <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a> while they were Ph.D. students at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>. Together they own about 14 percent of its shares and control 56 percent of the stockholder voting power through <a href="/wiki/Preferred_stock" title="Preferred stock">supervoting</a> stock. They incorporated Google as a California privately held company on September 4, 1998. Google was then reincorporated in Delaware on October 22, 2002.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[13]</a></sup> An initial public offering (IPO) took place on August 19, 2004, and Google moved to its headquarters in Mountain View, California, nicknamed the  <a href="/wiki/Googleplex" title="Googleplex">Googleplex</a>. In August 2015, Google announced plans to reorganize its various interests as a conglomerate called <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a> Google is Alphabet's leading subsidiary and will continue to be the umbrella company for Alphabet's Internet interests. <a href="/wiki/Sundar_Pichai" title="Sundar Pichai">Sundar Pichai</a> was appointed CEO of Google, replacing Larry Page, who became the CEO of Alphabet. In 2021, the <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Workers_Union" title="Alphabet Workers Union">Alphabet Workers Union</a> was founded, mainly composed of Google employees.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[14]</a></sup>
</p><p>The company's rapid growth since incorporation has triggered a chain of products, acquisitions, and partnerships beyond Google's core search engine (<a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google Search</a>). It offers services designed for work and productivity (<a href="/wiki/Google_Docs" title="Google Docs">Google Docs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Sheets" title="Google Sheets">Google Sheets</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Google_Slides" title="Google Slides">Google Slides</a>), email (<a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a>), scheduling and time management (<a href="/wiki/Google_Calendar" title="Google Calendar">Google Calendar</a>), cloud storage (<a href="/wiki/Google_Drive" title="Google Drive">Google Drive</a>), instant messaging and video chat (<a href="/wiki/Google_Duo" title="Google Duo">Duo</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hangouts" title="Hangouts">Hangouts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Chat" title="Google Chat">Chat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Google_Meet" title="Google Meet">Meet</a>), language translation (<a href="/wiki/Google_Translate" title="Google Translate">Google Translate</a>), mapping and navigation (<a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Waze" title="Waze">Waze</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Earth" title="Google Earth">Google Earth</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Street_View" title="Street View">Street View</a>), podcast hosting (<a href="/wiki/Google_Podcasts" title="Google Podcasts">Google Podcasts</a>), video sharing (<a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>), blog publishing (<a href="/wiki/Blogger_(service)" title="Blogger (service)">Blogger</a>), note-taking (<a href="/wiki/Google_Keep" title="Google Keep">Google Keep</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jamboard" title="Jamboard">Google Jamboard</a>), and photo organizing and editing (<a href="/wiki/Google_Photos" title="Google Photos">Google Photos</a>). The company leads the development of the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> mobile operating system, the <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a> web browser, and <a href="/wiki/Chrome_OS" title="Chrome OS">Chrome OS</a>, a lightweight operating system based on the Chrome browser. Google has moved increasingly into hardware; from 2010 to 2015, it partnered with major electronics manufacturers in the production of its <a href="/wiki/Google_Nexus" title="Google Nexus">Nexus</a> devices, and it released multiple hardware products in October 2016, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pixel_(smartphone)" title="Pixel (smartphone)">Google Pixel</a> line of smartphones, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Home" title="Google Home">Google Home</a> smart speaker, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_Wifi_(router)" title="Google Wifi (router)">Google Wifi</a> mesh wireless router, and <a href="/wiki/Google_Daydream" title="Google Daydream">Google Daydream</a> virtual reality headset. Google has also experimented with becoming an Internet carrier (<a href="/wiki/Google_Fiber" title="Google Fiber">Google Fiber</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Fi" title="Google Fi">Google Fi</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Google_Station" title="Google Station">Google Station</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Google.com is the most visited website worldwide. Several other Google-owned websites also are on the <a href="/wiki/List_of_most_popular_websites" title="List of most popular websites">list of most popular websites</a>, including YouTube and Blogger.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-topsites_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-topsites-17">[16]</a></sup>
</p><p>Google was the most valuable brand in the world in 2017 (surpassed by Amazon),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[17]</a></sup> but has received significant <a href="/wiki/Criticism_of_Google" title="Criticism of Google">criticism</a> involving issues such as <a href="/wiki/Privacy_concerns_regarding_Google" title="Privacy concerns regarding Google">privacy concerns</a>, tax avoidance, antitrust, <a href="/wiki/Censorship_by_Google" title="Censorship by Google">censorship</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Search_neutrality" title="Search neutrality">search neutrality</a>.
</p>
<div aria-labelledby="mw-toc-heading" class="toc" id="toc" role="navigation"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" dir="ltr" lang="en"><h2 id="mw-toc-heading">Contents</h2><span class="toctogglespan"><label class="toctogglelabel" for="toctogglecheckbox"></label></span></div>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Google" title="History of Google">History of Google</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_mergers_and_acquisitions_by_Alphabet" title="List of mergers and acquisitions by Alphabet">List of mergers and acquisitions by Alphabet</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet Inc.</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google_page_brin.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1073" data-file-width="1541" decoding="async" height="153" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Google_page_brin.jpg/220px-Google_page_brin.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Google_page_brin.jpg/330px-Google_page_brin.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0a/Google_page_brin.jpg/440px-Google_page_brin.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google_page_brin.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a> in 2003</div></div></div>
<p>Google began in January 1996 as a research project by <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sergey_Brin" title="Sergey Brin">Sergey Brin</a> when they were both PhD students at <a href="/wiki/Stanford_University" title="Stanford University">Stanford University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Stanford,_California" title="Stanford, California">Stanford, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milestones_19-0"><a href="#cite_note-milestones-19">[18]</a></sup> The project initially involved an unofficial "third founder", Scott Hassan, the original lead programmer who wrote much of the code for the original <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google Search</a> engine, but he left before Google was officially founded as a company;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vanityfair_20-0"><a href="#cite_note-vanityfair-20">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[20]</a></sup> Hassan went on to pursue a career in <a href="/wiki/Robotics" title="Robotics">robotics</a> and founded the company <a href="/wiki/Willow_Garage" title="Willow Garage">Willow Garage</a> in 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[21]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[22]</a></sup>
</p><p>While conventional search engines ranked results by counting how many times the search terms appeared on the page, they theorized about a better system that analyzed the relationships among websites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[23]</a></sup> They called this algorithm <a href="/wiki/PageRank" title="PageRank">PageRank</a>; it determined a website's <a href="/wiki/Relevance_(information_retrieval)" title="Relevance (information retrieval)">relevance</a> by the number of pages, and the importance of those pages that linked back to the original site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[24]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[25]</a></sup> Page told his ideas to Hassan, who began writing the code to implement Page's ideas.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-vanityfair_20-1"><a href="#cite_note-vanityfair-20">[19]</a></sup>
</p><p>Page and Brin originally nicknamed the new search engine "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/BackRub_(search_engine)" title="BackRub (search engine)">BackRub</a>", because the system checked backlinks to estimate the importance of a site.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[26]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[28]</a></sup> Hassan as well as Alan Steremberg were cited by Page and Brin as being critical to the development of Google. <a href="/wiki/Rajeev_Motwani" title="Rajeev Motwani">Rajeev Motwani</a> and <a href="/wiki/Terry_Winograd" title="Terry Winograd">Terry Winograd</a> later co-authored with Page and Brin the first paper about the project, describing PageRank and the initial prototype of the Google search engine, published in 1998. <a href="/wiki/H%C3%A9ctor_Garc%C3%ADa-Molina" title="Héctor García-Molina">Héctor García-Molina</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jeff_Ullman" title="Jeff Ullman">Jeff Ullman</a> were also cited as contributors to the project.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-originalpaper_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-originalpaper-30">[29]</a></sup> PageRank was influenced by a similar page-ranking and site-scoring algorithm earlier used for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/RankDex" title="RankDex">RankDex</a>, developed by <a href="/wiki/Robin_Li" title="Robin Li">Robin Li</a> in 1996, with Larry Page's PageRank patent including a citation to Li's earlier RankDex patent; Li later went on to create the Chinese search engine <a href="/wiki/Baidu" title="Baidu">Baidu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[32]</a></sup>
</p><p>Eventually, they changed the name to Google; the name of the search engine originated from a misspelling of the word "<a href="/wiki/Googol" title="Googol">googol</a>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[33]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[34]</a></sup> the number 1 followed by 100 zeros, which was picked to signify that the search engine was intended to provide large quantities of information.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google1998.png"><img alt="Google's homepage in 1998" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="235" data-file-width="423" decoding="async" height="139" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/Google1998.png/250px-Google1998.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b7/Google1998.png/375px-Google1998.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/b/b7/Google1998.png 2x" width="250"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google1998.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Google's original homepage had a simple design because the company founders had little experience in <a href="/wiki/HTML" title="HTML">HTML</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Markup_language" title="Markup language">markup language</a> used for designing web pages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[36]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The domain name <code>www.google.com</code> was registered on September 15, 1997,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[37]</a></sup> and the company was incorporated on September 4, 1998. It was based in the garage of a friend (<a href="/wiki/Susan_Wojcicki" title="Susan Wojcicki">Susan Wojcicki</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milestones_19-1"><a href="#cite_note-milestones-19">[18]</a></sup>) in <a href="/wiki/Menlo_Park,_California" title="Menlo Park, California">Menlo Park, California</a>. <a href="/wiki/Craig_Silverstein" title="Craig Silverstein">Craig Silverstein</a>, a fellow PhD student at Stanford, was hired as the first employee.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milestones_19-2"><a href="#cite_note-milestones-19">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[39]</a></sup>
</p><p>Google was initially funded by an August 1998 contribution of $100,000 from <a href="/wiki/Andy_Bechtolsheim" title="Andy Bechtolsheim">Andy Bechtolsheim</a>, co-founder of <a href="/wiki/Sun_Microsystems" title="Sun Microsystems">Sun Microsystems</a>; the money was given before Google was incorporated.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bechtolsheim_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bechtolsheim-41">[40]</a></sup> Google received money from three other <a href="/wiki/Angel_investor" title="Angel investor">angel investors</a> in 1998: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Amazon.com" title="Amazon.com">Amazon.com</a> founder <a href="/wiki/Jeff_Bezos" title="Jeff Bezos">Jeff Bezos</a>, Stanford University computer science professor <a href="/wiki/David_Cheriton" title="David Cheriton">David Cheriton</a>, and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Ram_Shriram" title="Ram Shriram">Ram Shriram</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-:3-42">[41]</a></sup> Between these initial investors, friends, and family Google raised around 1 million dollars, which is what allowed them to open up their original shop in <a href="/wiki/Menlo_Park,_California" title="Menlo Park, California">Menlo Park, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[42]</a></sup>
</p><p>After some additional, small investments through the end of 1998 to early 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:3_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-:3-42">[41]</a></sup> a new $25 million round of funding was announced on June 7, 1999,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[43]</a></sup> with major investors including the <a href="/wiki/Venture_capital" title="Venture capital">venture capital</a> firms <a href="/wiki/Kleiner_Perkins" title="Kleiner Perkins">Kleiner Perkins</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sequoia_Capital" title="Sequoia Capital">Sequoia Capital</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bechtolsheim_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-Bechtolsheim-41">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Growth">Growth</span></h3>
<p>In March 1999, the company moved its offices to <a href="/wiki/Palo_Alto,_California" title="Palo Alto, California">Palo Alto, California</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[44]</a></sup> which is home to several prominent <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Valley" title="Silicon Valley">Silicon Valley</a> technology start-ups.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[45]</a></sup> The next year, Google began selling advertisements associated with search keywords against Page and Brin's initial opposition toward an advertising-funded search engine.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-milestones_19-3"><a href="#cite_note-milestones-19">[18]</a></sup> To maintain an uncluttered page design, advertisements were solely text-based.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[47]</a></sup> In June 2000, it was announced that Google would become the default search engine provider for <a href="/wiki/Yahoo!" title="Yahoo!">Yahoo!</a>, one of the most popular websites at the time, replacing <a href="/wiki/Inktomi" title="Inktomi">Inktomi</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[49]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg"><img alt="Google's first servers, showing lots of exposed wiring and circuit boards" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="4209" data-file-width="2543" decoding="async" height="281" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg/170px-Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg/255px-Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg/340px-Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google%E2%80%99s_First_Production_Server.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Google's first production server.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[50]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>In 2003, after outgrowing two other locations, the company leased an office complex from <a href="/wiki/Silicon_Graphics" title="Silicon Graphics">Silicon Graphics</a>, at 1600 Amphitheatre Parkway in <a href="/wiki/Mountain_View,_California" title="Mountain View, California">Mountain View, California</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sgibldg_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-sgibldg-52">[51]</a></sup> The complex became known as the <a href="/wiki/Googleplex" title="Googleplex">Googleplex</a>, a play on the word <a href="/wiki/Googolplex" title="Googolplex">googolplex</a>, the number one followed by a googol zeroes. Three years later, Google bought the property from SGI for $319 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-googleplexpurchase_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-googleplexpurchase-53">[52]</a></sup> By that time, the name "Google" had found its way into everyday language, causing the verb "<a href="/wiki/Google_(verb)" title="Google (verb)">google</a>" to be added to the <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Merriam-Webster_Collegiate_Dictionary" title="Merriam-Webster Collegiate Dictionary">Merriam-Webster Collegiate Dictionary</a></i> and the <i><a href="/wiki/Oxford_English_Dictionary" title="Oxford English Dictionary">Oxford English Dictionary</a></i>, denoted as: "to use the Google search engine to obtain information on the Internet".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[53]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[54]</a></sup> Additionally, in 2001 Google's Investors felt the need to have a strong internal management, and they agreed to hire <a href="/wiki/Eric_Schmidt" title="Eric Schmidt">Eric Schmidt</a> as the Chairman and CEO of Google <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Google_Inc_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-Google_Inc-56">[55]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Initial_public_offering">Initial public offering</span></h3>
<p>Google's <a href="/wiki/Initial_public_offering" title="Initial public offering">initial public offering</a> (IPO) took place five years later, on August 19, 2004. At that time Larry Page, Sergey Brin, and Eric Schmidt agreed to work together at Google for 20 years, until the year 2024.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[56]</a></sup> At IPO, the company offered 19,605,052 shares at a price of $85 per share.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IPO_58-0"><a href="#cite_note-IPO-58">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:1_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-:1-59">[58]</a></sup> Shares were sold in an online auction format using a system built by <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Stanley" title="Morgan Stanley">Morgan Stanley</a> and <a href="/wiki/Credit_Suisse" title="Credit Suisse">Credit Suisse</a>, underwriters for the deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[60]</a></sup> The sale of $1.67 billion gave Google a <a href="/wiki/Market_capitalization" title="Market capitalization">market capitalization</a> of more than $23 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washpost_62-0"><a href="#cite_note-washpost-62">[61]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3541" data-file-width="2645" decoding="async" height="228" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg/170px-Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg/255px-Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg/340px-Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Eric_Schmidt_at_the_37th_G8_Summit_in_Deauville_037.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Eric_Schmidt" title="Eric Schmidt">Eric Schmidt</a>, CEO of Google from 2001 to 2011</div></div></div>
<p>In October 2006, Google announced that it had acquired the video-sharing site <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> for $1.65 billion in Google stock,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[63]</a></sup> and the deal was finalized on November 13, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[65]</a></sup> On April 13, 2007, Google reached an agreement to acquire <a href="/wiki/DoubleClick" title="DoubleClick">DoubleClick</a> for $3.1 billion, transferring to Google valuable relationships that DoubleClick had with Web publishers and advertising agencies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[66]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2005, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i> reported on a 700 percent increase in third-quarter profit for Google, largely thanks to large companies shifting their advertising strategies from newspapers, magazines, and television to the Internet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[67]</a></sup> In May 2011, the number of monthly unique visitors to Google surpassed one billion for the first time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[68]</a></sup> By 2011, Google was handling approximately 3 billion searches per day. To handle this workload, Google built 11 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Data_centers" title="Data centers">data centers</a> around the world with some several thousand servers in each. These data centers allowed Google to handle the ever changing workload more efficiently.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Google_Inc_56-1"><a href="#cite_note-Google_Inc-56">[55]</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 15, 2011, Google made its largest-ever acquisition to date when it announced that it would acquire <a href="/wiki/Motorola_Mobility" title="Motorola Mobility">Motorola Mobility</a> for $12.5 billion<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[70]</a></sup> This purchase was made in part to help Google gain Motorola's considerable patent portfolio on mobile phones and wireless technologies, to help protect Google in its ongoing patent disputes with other companies,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-supercharging_android_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-supercharging_android-72">[71]</a></sup> mainly <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple</a> and <a href="/wiki/Microsoft" title="Microsoft">Microsoft</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-appleinsider1_73-0"><a href="#cite_note-appleinsider1-73">[72]</a></sup> and to allow it to continue to freely offer <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cnet_74-0"><a href="#cite_note-cnet-74">[73]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2012_onward">2012 onward</span></h3>
<p>The year 2012 was the first time that Google generated $50 billion in annual revenue, generating $38 billion the previous year. In January 2013, then-CEO Larry Page commented, "We ended 2012 with a strong quarter ... Revenues were up 36% year-on-year, and 8% quarter-on-quarter. And we hit $50 billion in revenues for the first time last year – not a bad achievement in just a decade and a half."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[74]</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2013, Google acquired <a href="/wiki/Waze" title="Waze">Waze</a>, a $966 million deal.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[75]</a></sup> While Waze would remain an independent entity, its social features, such as its crowdsourced location platform, were reportedly valuable integrations between Waze and <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a>, Google's own mapping service.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[76]</a></sup>
</p><p>Google announced the launch of a new company, called <a href="/wiki/Calico_(company)" title="Calico (company)">Calico</a>, on September 19, 2013, to be led by <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a> chairman <a href="/wiki/Arthur_D._Levinson" title="Arthur D. Levinson">Arthur Levinson</a>. In the official public statement, Page explained that the "health and well-being" company would focus on "the challenge of ageing and associated diseases".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[77]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London,_6_Pancras_Square.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="2448" decoding="async" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London%2C_6_Pancras_Square.jpg/170px-Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London%2C_6_Pancras_Square.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London%2C_6_Pancras_Square.jpg/255px-Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London%2C_6_Pancras_Square.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London%2C_6_Pancras_Square.jpg/340px-Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London%2C_6_Pancras_Square.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Google-Deep_Mind_headquarters_in_London,_6_Pancras_Square.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Entrance of building where Google and its subsidiary Deep Mind are located at 6 Pancras Square, London</div></div></div>
<p>On January 26, 2014, Google announced it had agreed to acquire <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/DeepMind_Technologies" title="DeepMind Technologies">DeepMind Technologies</a>, a privately held artificial intelligence company from <a href="/wiki/London" title="London">London</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chowdhry-DeepMind_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chowdhry-DeepMind-79">[78]</a></sup> Technology news website <i><a href="/wiki/Recode" title="Recode">Recode</a></i> reported that the company was purchased for $400 million though it was not disclosed where the information came from. A Google spokesman would not comment of the price.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Helgren-_DeepMind_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-Helgren-_DeepMind-80">[79]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ribeiro-_DeepMind_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ribeiro-_DeepMind-81">[80]</a></sup> The purchase of DeepMind aids in Google's recent growth in the artificial intelligence and robotics community.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[81]</a></sup>
</p><p>According to <a href="/wiki/Interbrand" title="Interbrand">Interbrand</a>'s annual Best Global Brands report, Google has been the second most valuable brand in the world (behind <a href="/wiki/Apple_Inc." title="Apple Inc.">Apple Inc.</a>) in 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[82]</a></sup> 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[83]</a></sup> 2015,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85">[84]</a></sup> and 2016, with a valuation of $133 billion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[85]</a></sup>
</p><p>On August 10, 2015, Google announced plans to reorganize its various interests as a <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">conglomerate</a> called <a href="/wiki/Alphabet_Inc." title="Alphabet Inc.">Alphabet</a>. Google became Alphabet's leading subsidiary, and will continue to be the umbrella company for Alphabet's Internet interests. Upon completion of the restructure, <a href="/wiki/Sundar_Pichai" title="Sundar Pichai">Sundar Pichai</a> became CEO of Google, replacing <a href="/wiki/Larry_Page" title="Larry Page">Larry Page</a>, who became CEO of Alphabet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[88]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_CEO_of_Google,_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister,_Shri_Narendra_Modi,_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17,_2015_(1).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1524" data-file-width="2200" decoding="async" height="152" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/The_CEO_of_Google%2C_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17%2C_2015_%281%29.jpg/220px-The_CEO_of_Google%2C_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17%2C_2015_%281%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/The_CEO_of_Google%2C_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17%2C_2015_%281%29.jpg/330px-The_CEO_of_Google%2C_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17%2C_2015_%281%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5b/The_CEO_of_Google%2C_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17%2C_2015_%281%29.jpg/440px-The_CEO_of_Google%2C_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister%2C_Shri_Narendra_Modi%2C_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17%2C_2015_%281%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_CEO_of_Google,_Mr._Sundar_Pichai_calls_on_the_Prime_Minister,_Shri_Narendra_Modi,_in_New_Delhi_on_December_17,_2015_(1).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Current Google CEO, <a href="/wiki/Sundar_Pichai" title="Sundar Pichai">Sundar Pichai</a>, with Prime Minister of India, <a href="/wiki/Narendra_Modi" title="Narendra Modi">Narendra Modi</a></div></div></div>
<p>On August 8, 2017, Google fired employee <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Damore" title="James Damore">James Damore</a> after he distributed a memo throughout the company which argued that bias and "<a href="/wiki/Google%27s_Ideological_Echo_Chamber" title="Google's Ideological Echo Chamber">Google's ideological echo chamber</a>" clouded their thinking about diversity and inclusion, and that it is also biological factors, not discrimination alone, that cause the average woman to be less interested than men in technical positions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYTFired_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYTFired-90">[89]</a></sup> Google CEO Sundar Pichai accused Damore in violating company policy by "advancing harmful gender stereotypes in our workplace", and he was fired on the same day.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93">[92]</a></sup> <i>New York Times</i> columnist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Brooks_(political_commentator)" title="David Brooks (political commentator)">David Brooks</a> argued Pichai had mishandled the case, and called for his resignation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BrooksNYT_94-0"><a href="#cite_note-BrooksNYT-94">[93]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[94]</a></sup>
</p><p>Between 2018 and 2019, <a href="/wiki/Google_worker_organization" title="Google worker organization">tensions between the company's leadership and its workers escalated</a> as staff protested company decisions on internal sexual harassment, <a href="/wiki/Dragonfly_(search_engine)" title="Dragonfly (search engine)">a censored Chinese search engine</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Project_Maven" title="Project Maven">a military drone artificial intelligence</a>, which had been seen as areas of revenue growth for the company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bloomberg_2019-11-22_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bloomberg_2019-11-22-96">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verge_busting_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-Verge_busting-97">[96]</a></sup> On October 25, 2018, <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> published the <i>exposé</i>, "How Google Protected <a href="/wiki/Andy_Rubin" title="Andy Rubin">Andy Rubin</a>, the ‘Father of Android’". The company subsequently announced that "48 employees have been fired over the last two years" for sexual misconduct.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[97]</a></sup> On November 1, 2018, more than 20,000 Google employees and contractors staged a global walk-out to protest the company's handling of sexual harassment complaints.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[98]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[99]</a></sup> Later in 2019, some workers accused the company of retaliating against internal activists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Verge_busting_97-1"><a href="#cite_note-Verge_busting-97">[96]</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 19, 2019, Google announced that it would enter the video game market, launching a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_gaming" title="Cloud gaming">cloud gaming</a> platform called <a href="/wiki/Google_Stadia" title="Google Stadia">Stadia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-101">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>On June 3, 2019, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> reported that it would investigate Google for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Antitrust" title="Antitrust">antitrust</a> violations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[101]</a></sup> This led to the filing of an antitrust lawsuit in October 2020, on the grounds the company had abused a monopoly position in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Web_search_engine" title="Web search engine">search</a> and <a href="/wiki/Search_advertising" title="Search advertising">search advertising</a> markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[102]</a></sup>
</p><p>In December 2019, it was reported that former <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chief_Operating_Officer" title="Chief Operating Officer">Chief Operating Officer</a> Bill Ready would become Google's new commerce chief. Ready's role will not be directly involved with <a href="/wiki/Google_Pay" title="Google Pay">Google Pay</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[103]</a></sup>
</p><p>In April 2020, due to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic" title="COVID-19 pandemic">COVID-19 pandemic</a>, Google announced several cost-cutting measures. Such measures included slowing down hiring for the remainder of 2020, except for a small number of strategic areas, recalibrating the focus and pace of investments in areas like data centers and machines, and non-business essential marketing and travel. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[104]</a></sup>
</p><p>Also in 2020, <a href="/wiki/2020_Google_services_outages" title="2020 Google services outages">three worldwide outages</a> occurred that disrupted Google services: one in August that affected Google Drive among others, another in November affecting YouTube, and a third in December affecting the entire suite of Google applications. All three outages were resolved within hours. <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[107]</a></sup>
</p><p>In January 2021, the Australian government proposed legislation that would require Google and Facebook to pay media companies for the right to use their content. In response, Google threatened to close off access to its search engine in Australia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[108]</a></sup>
</p><p>In March 2021, Google reportedly paid $20m for <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft" title="Ubisoft">Ubisoft</a> ports on <a href="/wiki/Google_Stadia" title="Google Stadia">Stadia.</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[109]</a></sup> Google spent "tens of millions of dollars" on getting major publishers such as <a href="/wiki/Ubisoft" title="Ubisoft">Ubisoft</a> and Take-Two to bring some of their biggest games to Stadia. 
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Products_and_services">Products and services</span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_Google_products" title="List of Google products">List of Google products</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Search_engine">Search engine</span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google Search</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Images" title="Google Images">Google Images</a></div>
<p>Google <a href="/wiki/Search_engine_indexing" title="Search engine indexing">indexes</a> billions of web pages to allow users to search for the information they desire through the use of keywords and <a href="/wiki/Operator_(computer_programming)" title="Operator (computer programming)">operators</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[110]</a></sup> According to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ComScore" title="ComScore">comScore</a> market research from November 2009, <a href="/wiki/Google_Search" title="Google Search">Google Search</a> is the dominant search engine in the United States market, with a <a href="/wiki/Market_share" title="Market share">market share</a> of 65.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-comscore_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-comscore-112">[111]</a></sup> In May 2017, Google enabled a new "Personal" tab in Google Search, letting users search for content in their Google accounts' various services, including email messages from <a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a> and photos from <a href="/wiki/Google_Photos" title="Google Photos">Google Photos</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[112]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[113]</a></sup>
</p><p>Google launched its <a href="/wiki/Google_News" title="Google News">Google News</a> service in 2002, an automated service which summarizes news articles from various websites.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115">[114]</a></sup> Google also hosts <a href="/wiki/Google_Books" title="Google Books">Google Books</a>, a service which searches the text found in books in its database and shows limited previews or and the full book where allowed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[115]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Advertising">Advertising</span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ad-tech_London_2010_(2).JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2448" data-file-width="3264" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ad-tech_London_2010_%282%29.JPG/220px-Ad-tech_London_2010_%282%29.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ad-tech_London_2010_%282%29.JPG/330px-Ad-tech_London_2010_%282%29.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Ad-tech_London_2010_%282%29.JPG/440px-Ad-tech_London_2010_%282%29.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ad-tech_London_2010_(2).JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Google on ad-tech London, 2010</div></div></div>
<p>As per its 2017 Annual report, Google generates most of its revenues from advertising. This includes sales of apps, purchases made in-app, digital content products on Google and YouTube, Android and licensing and service fees, including fees received for Google Cloud offerings. Forty-six percent of this profit was from clicks (cost per clicks), amounting to US$109,652 million in 2017. This includes three principal methods, namely <a href="/wiki/AdMob" title="AdMob">AdMob</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AdSense" title="AdSense">AdSense</a> (such as AdSense for Content, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AdSense" title="AdSense">AdSense</a> for Search, etc.) and DoubleClick AdExchange.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-agm2017_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-agm2017-117">[116]</a></sup>
</p><p>For the 2006 fiscal year, the company reported $10.492 billion in total advertising revenues and only $112 million in licensing and other revenues.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10-K_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-10-K-118">[117]</a></sup> In 2011, 96% of Google's revenue was derived from its advertising programs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Google-Inc-Jan-2012-10-K_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-Google-Inc-Jan-2012-10-K-119">[118]</a></sup> In addition to its own algorithms for understanding search requests, Google uses technology from the company <a href="/wiki/DoubleClick" title="DoubleClick">DoubleClick</a>, to project user interest and target advertising to the search context and the user history.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[119]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121">[120]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2007, Google launched "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AdSense_for_Mobile" title="AdSense for Mobile">AdSense for Mobile</a>", taking advantage of the emerging mobile advertising market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adsense_mobile_122-0"><a href="#cite_note-adsense_mobile-122">[121]</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Google_Analytics" title="Google Analytics">Google Analytics</a> allows website owners to track where and how people use their website, for example by examining click rates for all the links on a page.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[122]</a></sup> Google advertisements can be placed on third-party websites in a two-part program. <a href="/wiki/Google_Ads" title="Google Ads">Google Ads</a> allows advertisers to display their advertisements in the Google content network, through a cost-per-click scheme.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[123]</a></sup> The sister service, Google <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AdSense" title="AdSense">AdSense</a>, allows website owners to display these advertisements on their website and earn money every time ads are clicked.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[124]</a></sup> One of the criticisms of this program is the possibility of <a href="/wiki/Click_fraud" title="Click fraud">click fraud</a>, which occurs when a person or automated script clicks on advertisements without being interested in the product, causing the advertiser to pay money to Google unduly. Industry reports in 2006 claimed that approximately 14 to 20 percent of clicks were fraudulent or invalid.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[125]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Search_Console" title="Google Search Console">Google Search Console</a> (rebranded from Google Webmaster Tools in May 2015) allows <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Webmasters" title="Webmasters">webmasters</a> to check the sitemap, crawl rate, and for security issues of their websites, as well as optimize their website's visibility.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Consumer_services">Consumer services</span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Web-based_services">Web-based services</span></h4>
<p>Google offers <a href="/wiki/Gmail" title="Gmail">Gmail</a> for <a href="/wiki/Email" title="Email">email</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[126]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Calendar" title="Google Calendar">Google Calendar</a> for time-management and scheduling,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[127]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Maps" title="Google Maps">Google Maps</a> for mapping, navigation and <a href="/wiki/Satellite_imagery" title="Satellite imagery">satellite imagery</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129">[128]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Drive" title="Google Drive">Google Drive</a> for <a href="/wiki/File_hosting_service" title="File hosting service">cloud storage</a> of files,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-drive-announced_130-0"><a href="#cite_note-verge-drive-announced-130">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Docs" title="Google Docs">Google Docs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Google_Sheets" title="Google Sheets">Sheets</a> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Slides" title="Google Slides">Slides</a> for productivity,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-verge-drive-announced_130-1"><a href="#cite_note-verge-drive-announced-130">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Photos" title="Google Photos">Google Photos</a> for photo storage and sharing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131">[130]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Keep" title="Google Keep">Google Keep</a> for <a href="/wiki/Note-taking" title="Note-taking">note-taking</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[131]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Google_Translate" title="Google Translate">Google Translate</a> for language translation,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[132]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> for video viewing and sharing,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[133]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Google_My_Business" title="Google My Business">Google My Business</a> for managing public business information,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135">[134]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Google_Duo" title="Google Duo">Duo</a> for social interaction.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136">[135]</a></sup> In March 2019, Google unveiled a <a href="/wiki/Cloud_gaming" title="Cloud gaming">cloud gaming</a> service named <a href="/wiki/Google_Stadia" title="Google Stadia">Stadia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_101-1"><a href="#cite_note-:2-101">[100]</a></sup>
</p><p>Some Google services are not web-based. <a href="/wiki/Google_Earth" title="Google Earth">Google Earth</a>, launched in 2005, allowed users to see high-definition satellite pictures from all over the world for free through a client software downloaded to their computers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137">[136]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Software">Software</span></h4>
<p>Google develops the <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> <a href="/wiki/Mobile_operating_system" title="Mobile operating system">mobile operating system</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[137]</a></sup> as well as its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Android_Wear" title="Android Wear">smartwatch</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[138]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Android_TV" title="Android TV">television</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[139]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Android_Auto" title="Android Auto">car</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[140]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Internet_of_things" title="Internet of things">Internet of things</a>-enabled <a href="/wiki/Android_Things" title="Android Things">smart devices</a> variations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[141]</a></sup>
</p><p>It also develops the <a href="/wiki/Google_Chrome" title="Google Chrome">Google Chrome</a> web browser,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[142]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Chrome_OS" title="Chrome OS">Chrome OS</a>, an operating system based on Chrome.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[143]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Hardware">Hardware</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Pixel_3_%E3%81%A8_Pixel_3_XL_%E3%82%92%E5%88%9D%E8%A7%A6%E3%80%82%E6%9C%AC%E4%BD%93%E3%82%92%E3%82%AE%E3%83%A5%E3%83%83%E3%81%A8%E6%8F%A1%E3%82%8B%E3%81%A8_Google_Assistant_%E3%81%8C%E7%AB%8B%E3%81%A1%E4%B8%8A%E3%81%8C%E3%82%8B%E3%81%AE%E3%81%8C%E3%81%8A%E3%82%82%E3%81%97%E3%82%8D%E3%81%84%E3%80%82_%E3%83%AF%E3%82%B7%E3%83%B3%E3%83%88%E3%83%B3DC_(44519013945).jpg"><img
